## Section 001: Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not define how to select, sequence, and verify Rust idioms for a library, CLI, service, async worker, or refactor with different API, ownership, concurrency, and compatibility risks
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Rust's compiler prevents many classes of misuse but cannot choose product invariants, error semantics, task ownership, lock granularity, dependency direction, test depth, or operational evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the checklist is applied mechanically, generic traits or `AsRef` obscure APIs, cloning is removed at readability cost, async is introduced without need, all-feature gates conflict with the workspace, or compile success substitutes for behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for general Rust design review and route backend, embedded, unsafe, FFI, cryptography, or framework specifics to dedicated evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add task classification, causal idiom selection, counterexamples, compatibility and feature boundaries, staged alternatives, operational examples, and claim-linked verification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that idiomatic Rust is not maximum type or trait sophistication; it is the smallest design that makes ownership, invalid states, failure, and concurrency obligations visible
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to model invariants in types, expose borrowed and domain-shaped APIs, keep errors actionable, own async cancellation and backpressure, minimize lock scope and unnecessary cloning, preserve dependency boundaries, and prove claims with repository-aligned tests and gates
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Rust's compiler prevents many classes of misuse but cannot choose product invariants, error semantics, task ownership, lock granularity, dependency direction, test depth, or operational evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the checklist is applied mechanically, generic traits or `AsRef` obscure APIs, cloning is removed at readability cost, async is introduced without need, all-feature gates conflict with the workspace, or compile success substitutes for behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this reference for general Rust design review and route backend, embedded, unsafe, FFI, cryptography, or framework specifics to dedicated evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add task classification, causal idiom selection, counterexamples, compatibility and feature boundaries, staged alternatives, operational examples, and claim-linked verification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies idiomatic Rust is not maximum type or trait sophistication; it is the smallest design that makes ownership, invalid states, failure, and concurrency obligations visible
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the crate role and MSRV are known, callers and failure modes are identifiable, concurrency and performance claims are bounded, repository commands are available, and changes can be tested at the right layer
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because Rust's compiler prevents many classes of misuse but cannot choose product invariants, error semantics, task ownership, lock granularity, dependency direction, test depth, or operational evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where the checklist is applied mechanically, generic traits or `AsRef` obscure APIs, cloning is removed at readability cost, async is introduced without need, all-feature gates conflict with the workspace, or compile success substitutes for behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by use this reference for general Rust design review and route backend, embedded, unsafe, FFI, cryptography, or framework specifics to dedicated evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the crate role and MSRV are known, callers and failure modes are identifiable, concurrency and performance claims are bounded, repository commands are available, and changes can be tested at the right layer
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that idiomatic Rust is not maximum type or trait sophistication; it is the smallest design that makes ownership, invalid states, failure, and concurrency obligations visible
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the checklist is applied mechanically, generic traits or `AsRef` obscure APIs, cloning is removed at readability cost, async is introduced without need, all-feature gates conflict with the workspace, or compile success substitutes for behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are newtypes without validation, `anyhow` leaking into libraries, locks across await, unbounded channels, cancellation orphaning effects, `Arc` used by habit, traits with one unneeded implementation, and benchmarks without constraints
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the crate role and MSRV are known, callers and failure modes are identifiable, concurrency and performance claims are bounded, repository commands are available, and changes can be tested at the right layer
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using use this reference for general Rust design review and route backend, embedded, unsafe, FFI, cryptography, or framework specifics to dedicated evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: keep a concrete API until callers demand abstraction, use owned values at real ownership boundaries, remain synchronous, use a focused test and feature set, preserve existing error conventions, or isolate legacy design behind typed adapters
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the two local paths are duplicate copies, external sources were not refreshed, and the checklist cannot define current crate APIs, project MSRV, framework behavior, or performance budgets

- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: keep a concrete API until callers demand abstraction, use owned values at real ownership boundaries, remain synchronous, use a focused test and feature set, preserve existing error conventions, or isolate legacy design behind typed adapters

### Question 07: What do good, bad, and borderline examples look like?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the operational comparison is Good: a library parses a newtype with `TryFrom`, exposes `&str`, returns contextual variants, and property-tests invariants. Bad: add generic conversions and clones everywhere. Borderline: `Arc<Mutex<_>>` is valid only when shared ownership and critical sections are explicit and stress-tested

- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Idioms Checklist Patterns", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that idiomatic Rust is not maximum type or trait sophistication; it is the smallest design that makes ownership, invalid states, failure, and concurrency obligations visible

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists two byte-identical monthly copies of one checklist plus API, Tokio, and Axum sources, while the checklist itself names two unavailable absolute-path source bases
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because duplicate files do not corroborate, absent upstreams cannot be audited, and framework repositories cannot establish universal Rust design guidance
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: two copies become two votes, inaccessible downloads are presented as verified, Axum examples govern non-web crates, Tokio design implies all async code, or external source prestige replaces local needs
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the six frozen rows only to capable claims and treat project code, MSRV, Cargo features, and tests as direct evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add duplicate-lineage handling, unavailable-upstream warning, claim-specific authority, locked-version gates, counterexamples, and a provenance ledger
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that source lineage matters because a compact checklist is synthesis evidence, not independent proof of every idiom it contains
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat the two local rows as one checklist lineage, preserve its inaccessible upstream references as a provenance limitation, use API Guidelines for applicable public API claims, and use Tokio or Axum only for locked-version ecosystem mechanics
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because duplicate files do not corroborate, absent upstreams cannot be audited, and framework repositories cannot establish universal Rust design guidance
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; two copies become two votes, inaccessible downloads are presented as verified, Axum examples govern non-web crates, Tokio design implies all async code, or external source prestige replaces local needs

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed says to combine local and external evidence with verification but does not explain that idioms are tools for making invariants, ownership, failure, concurrency, and dependency obligations explicit
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Rust syntax and compiler checks constrain possibilities but cannot decide domain types, abstraction cost, cancellation semantics, lock scope, error context, or test sufficiency
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: idiomatic becomes more generics, fewer clones at any cost, universal async, traits without seams, one error crate everywhere, or all-feature commands applied regardless of workspace design
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the thesis to general safe Rust and route unsafe, FFI, embedded, cryptographic, framework, and distributed concerns to dedicated guidance
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic synthesis with obligation mapping, smallest-fit alternatives, counterexamples, semver and compatibility limits, and layered verification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that idiomatic design minimizes hidden contracts, not necessarily type count, line count, cloning count, or abstraction depth

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed frames adopt, adapt, and avoid around source agreement rather than Rust choices among borrowed and owned data, concrete and generic APIs, newtypes, typed and contextual errors, sync and async, cloning, shared ownership, traits, and layers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each idiom exchanges ergonomics, compile time, semver surface, allocation, indirection, runtime complexity, and testability
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: source agreement triggers generic APIs, adaptation means cloning everywhere, avoidance leaves panics, or elegance outranks stable callers and tests
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: decide per API and lifecycle, not through repository-wide slogans

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed verifies seven document-shape elements but does not prove that the reference covers API callers, invalid states, conversions, typed failures, async cancellation, bounded work, dependency direction, compatibility, documentation, or measured claims
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a structurally complete document can still conceal the exact contracts that make an apparently idiomatic Rust choice correct or dangerous
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: completion is inferred from section presence, Clippy cleanliness, compilation, or a polished example while panic paths, cancellation, public compatibility, or unsupported claims remain unexamined
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the full gate to public, concurrent, cross-layer, or measured changes; scale it down explicitly for private syntax-preserving edits
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the seven generic document checks with an evidence-indexed completion gate spanning source, behavior, lifecycle, compatibility, verification, and routing

## Section 017: Adjacent Reference Routing
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed correctly says to hand off backend delivery, executable specifications, and quality gates but then supplies three tautological rust, idioms, and checklist placeholders that do not identify a destination, trigger, or return condition
- **supporting_reason:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing by governing obligation prevents a broad checklist from inventing protocol, deployment, security, or executable-spec details that require their own evidence and verification
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing is based only on a Rust keyword, several references appear equally valid without precedence, the target is unavailable, or the handoff discards caller and failure evidence already collected

- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic adjacent labels with a trigger-to-destination table, precedence rules, handoff payload, unavailable-route fallback, and return checklist
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that routing is an evidence-preserving state transition rather than a link list; ownership and return criteria matter as much as destination names
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to stay here for API shape, conversions, errors, ownership, async hygiene, layering, tests, documentation, and review questions; route requirements to rust_executable_reference_maps, HTTP delivery to rust_backend_reference_routing, release checks to rust_conventions_quality_gates or rust_quality_gate_patterns, and threat or resilience controls to rust_backend_security_resilience

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; routing is based only on a Rust keyword, several references appear equally valid without precedence, the target is unavailable, or the handoff discards caller and failure evidence already collected

- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace generic adjacent labels with a trigger-to-destination table, precedence rules, handoff payload, unavailable-route fallback, and return checklist
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies routing is an evidence-preserving state transition rather than a link list; ownership and return criteria matter as much as destination names

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed usefully frames systems implementation, CLI or service hardening, async review, one bounded workspace slice, and an integration path, but its fixed 100-symbol ceiling is ungrounded and its source-pressure row truncates the local checklist
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because review cost grows faster with ownership, concurrency, compatibility, and effect boundaries than with raw symbol or line counts
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a nominally small patch changes a public enum, cancellation semantics, feature resolution, or unsafe boundary; alternatively, a large mechanical private edit is split solely because it crosses an arbitrary symbol count
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this model guides checklist application; production capacity, security scope, and migration choreography require specialized workload and service evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the fixed symbol threshold and truncated source row with an obligation inventory, risk multipliers, explicit split triggers, workload examples, and evidence-based boundary adjustment
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the useful unit of Rust review is a coherent set of obligations whose failure and rollback can be tested together, not a fixed quantity of changed syntax
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to scope work by contract crossings: affected crates and public items, downstream callers, state transitions, error variants, spawned tasks, locks and channels, external effects, dependency-layer changes, feature sets, MSRV targets, documentation examples, and required integration paths

- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace the fixed symbol threshold and truncated source row with an obligation inventory, risk multipliers, explicit split triggers, workload examples, and evidence-based boundary adjustment

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed establishes source-label preservation, sampled routing accuracy, zero unsupported operational claims, and recovery clarity, but its 18-of-20 decision threshold has no baseline and the targets omit API, panic, error, cancellation, feature, documentation, and dependency outcomes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a reference can preserve labels and still recommend an API that burdens callers or an async pattern that leaks work, so reliability must cover decisions and lifecycle outcomes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a tiny convenience sample produces a percentage, reviewers know the expected answer, several findings share one root cause, deterministic checks are averaged with judgment calls, or a target lacks a response when breached
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: these targets assess use of the idioms reference; service availability, security assurance, and business correctness need dedicated objectives and telemetry
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain mechanically auditable source and claim invariants, replace the fixed sampled threshold with a baseline-relative protocol, and add obligation-specific outcome targets with breach responses
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reference reliability is the probability that its advice preserves the governing contract under realistic callers and failure paths, not the proportion of rows that look complete
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat complete evidence labeling and zero unsupported production claims as deterministic release invariants, then set baseline-relative sampled targets for correct routing, public API rework, invalid-state escape, panic exposure, error-context retention, cancellation, bounded work, feature and MSRV compatibility, dependency direction, docs, and recovery clarity

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed names source drift, generic advice, runtime contention, and production panic, but it omits overgeneralized APIs, representable invalid states, lost error context, blocking async work, locks across await, unbounded queues, missing cancellation, clone-heavy hot paths, layer inversion, ornamental traits, feature regressions, stale docs, and unmeasured optimization
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because different symptoms can share a cause and similar symptoms can require opposite fixes; causal classification prevents reflexive rewrites such as adding traits, clones, retries, or locks
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: warnings are style slogans, mitigation repeats the preferred idiom without diagnosis, rollback cannot restore public compatibility, concurrency tests omit shutdown, or the table treats compiler success as evidence that runtime and caller contracts hold
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry covers idiom and review failures; exploit analysis, distributed consistency, database recovery, and service incident response need narrower evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand four broad rows into a causal registry spanning API, state, error, async, ownership, architecture, compatibility, testing, docs, and unsupported claims, with detection and rollback columns
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the most dangerous idiom failures are hidden contract transfers, where convenience in one function pushes panic, ownership, queueing, or compatibility cost onto callers and operators

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed usefully limits stale-evidence refresh, stops work on red gates, checkpoints long workflows, and assigns one file owner, but it conflates reference-generation retries with application retries and leaves idempotency, attempt budgets, deadlines, queue capacity, cancellation, and overload evidence implicit
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retry converts time and capacity into another chance of success, so an unclassified retry can duplicate effects, lengthen shutdown, saturate a queue, or make a persistent defect look intermittent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: compiler errors, panics, invariant violations, deterministic test assertions, authorization failures, or schema incompatibilities are retried; a side effect lacks a deduplication key; or new work enters faster than bounded consumers can drain it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to separate evidence replay from runtime retry, add a retryability decision record and stop conditions, and connect workflow backpressure to bounded channels, cancellation, overload telemetry, and handoff rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify the failure first; replay a flaky observation only under a bounded diagnostic budget, refresh stale evidence once, fix deterministic code or assertion failures instead of retrying, and route production retry policy to a backend reference that can prove idempotency, deadlines, capacity, cancellation, and service-specific limits
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because retry converts time and capacity into another chance of success, so an unclassified retry can duplicate effects, lengthen shutdown, saturate a queue, or make a persistent defect look intermittent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; compiler errors, panics, invariant violations, deterministic test assertions, authorization failures, or schema incompatibilities are retried; a side effect lacks a deduplication key; or new work enters faster than bounded consumers can drain it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: separate evidence replay from runtime retry, add a retryability decision record and stop conditions, and connect workflow backpressure to bounded channels, cancellation, overload telemetry, and handoff rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the policy records failure class, retryable operation, idempotency basis, maximum attempts, total deadline, delay strategy, queue capacity, cancellation behavior, telemetry, terminal error, owner, and escalation or rollback
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because retry converts time and capacity into another chance of success, so an unclassified retry can duplicate effects, lengthen shutdown, saturate a queue, or make a persistent defect look intermittent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where compiler errors, panics, invariant violations, deterministic test assertions, authorization failures, or schema incompatibilities are retried; a side effect lacks a deduplication key; or new work enters faster than bounded consumers can drain it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the policy records failure class, retryable operation, idempotency basis, maximum attempts, total deadline, delay strategy, queue capacity, cancellation behavior, telemetry, terminal error, owner, and escalation or rollback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: compiler errors, panics, invariant violations, deterministic test assertions, authorization failures, or schema incompatibilities are retried; a side effect lacks a deduplication key; or new work enters faster than bounded consumers can drain it
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are timeouts after a successful remote effect, nested library and application retries, cancellation between effect and acknowledgment, jitter that exceeds a parent deadline, bounded channel capacity without bounded producers, and retries that erase the first error chain
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the policy records failure class, retryable operation, idempotency basis, maximum attempts, total deadline, delay strategy, queue capacity, cancellation behavior, telemetry, terminal error, owner, and escalation or rollback
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: fail fast with typed context, quarantine a flaky test, pause producers, shed optional work, reduce concurrency, use a dead-letter or manual review path, roll back a change, or narrow the evidence question
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the corpus does not define transport semantics, idempotency storage, service latency budgets, queue capacities, retry intervals, or production overload targets
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: fail fast with typed context, quarantine a flaky test, pause producers, shed optional work, reduce concurrency, use a dead-letter or manual review path, roll back a change, or narrow the evidence question
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare those alternatives against the decision to determine when a failed evidence, test, tool, or runtime operation may be retried and what mechanism prevents retries from hiding deterministic defects or amplifying load
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: alternatives become option theater when timeouts after a successful remote effect, nested library and application retries, cancellation between effect and acknowledgment, jitter that exceeds a parent deadline, bounded channel capacity without bounded producers, and retries that erase the first error chain
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare only choices allowed by this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: revise the guidance to contrast the default with each viable recovery and apply this section-specific change: separate evidence replay from runtime retry, add a retryability decision record and stop conditions, and connect workflow backpressure to bounded channels, cancellation, overload telemetry, and handoff rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: make the tradeoff consequential by connecting it to backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 06: Which gotchas and failure modes matter most?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: the highest-value warnings are timeouts after a successful remote effect, nested library and application retries, cancellation between effect and acknowledgment, jitter that exceeds a parent deadline, bounded channel capacity without bounded producers, and retries that erase the first error chain
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: these warnings deserve priority because compiler errors, panics, invariant violations, deterministic test assertions, authorization failures, or schema incompatibilities are retried; a side effect lacks a deduplication key; or new work enters faster than bounded consumers can drain it
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: do not classify ordinary variation as failure when the policy records failure class, retryable operation, idempotency basis, maximum attempts, total deadline, delay strategy, queue capacity, cancellation behavior, telemetry, terminal error, owner, and escalation or rollback
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: evaluate each warning inside this assumption set: this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: add observable warning signs plus the recovery path fail fast with typed context, quarantine a flaky test, pause producers, shed optional work, reduce concurrency, use a dead-letter or manual review path, roll back a change, or narrow the evidence question
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: explain the systemic effect that backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 07: What do good, bad, and borderline examples look like?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the operational comparison is Good: rerun one suspected timing-sensitive stress fixture with seed and scheduler details, then quarantine and investigate if it diverges. Bad: loop cargo test until green. Borderline: retry an idempotent read within a parent deadline only after a specialized backend policy defines attempts and overload behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the good case is credible because the policy records failure class, retryable operation, idempotency basis, maximum attempts, total deadline, delay strategy, queue capacity, cancellation behavior, telemetry, terminal error, owner, and escalation or rollback
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the borderline case must expose the limit that the corpus does not define transport semantics, idempotency storage, service latency budgets, queue capacities, retry intervals, or production overload targets
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: interpret all three examples within this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: revise the examples so each reveals a decision, consequence, and recovery while implementing this section-specific change: separate evidence replay from runtime retry, add a retryability decision record and stop conditions, and connect workflow backpressure to bounded channels, cancellation, overload telemetry, and handoff rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: use the comparison to surface this deeper lesson: backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 08: How can the important claims be verified?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: verify the important claims by doing the following: inject each classified failure, count attempts and elapsed budget, observe queue depth and cancellation, prove duplicate effects are prevented where relevant, preserve first and terminal errors, test overload and shutdown, and confirm deterministic failures stop immediately
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: this evidence is appropriate because the seed directly supports classification, one bounded refresh, red-gate backpressure, checkpointing, and ownership; the local checklist supports bounded channels, cancellation, stress testing, and explicit errors
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: verification cannot erase the judgment that the corpus does not define transport semantics, idempotency storage, service latency budgets, queue capacities, retry intervals, or production overload targets
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: reject evidence gathered outside this boundary: this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: add pass/fail observations tied to the revision separate evidence replay from runtime retry, add a retryability decision record and stop conditions, and connect workflow backpressure to bounded channels, cancellation, overload telemetry, and handoff rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: verification should also test the consequence that backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 09: What is known confidently, and what remains judgment or uncertainty?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the confident evidence is the seed directly supports classification, one bounded refresh, red-gate backpressure, checkpointing, and ownership; the local checklist supports bounded channels, cancellation, stress testing, and explicit errors
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the retained seed basis is transient-versus-stale classification, one bounded evidence refresh, stopping new work on red gates, frequent checkpoints, sole ownership, and merge-time path checks remain preserved

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: label direct evidence, inference, and provisional guidance separately while implementing separate evidence replay from runtime retry, add a retryability decision record and stop conditions, and connect workflow backpressure to bounded channels, cancellation, overload telemetry, and handoff rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: preserve uncertainty because it affects the deduction that backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
### Question 10: What deeper deductions, second-order consequences, or additional insights follow, and how should they change the guidance?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that backpressure is part of correctness because it preserves the system's ability to reject and explain work before resource exhaustion destroys the evidence needed for diagnosis
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from retry converts time and capacity into another chance of success, so an unclassified retry can duplicate effects, lengthen shutdown, saturate a queue, or make a persistent defect look intermittent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where compiler errors, panics, invariant violations, deterministic test assertions, authorization failures, or schema incompatibilities are retried; a side effect lacks a deduplication key; or new work enters faster than bounded consumers can drain it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within this section governs reference workflow and generic Rust lifecycle hygiene; production network, database, and queue retries require protocol-specific reliability evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: separate evidence replay from runtime retry, add a retryability decision record and stop conditions, and connect workflow backpressure to bounded channels, cancellation, overload telemetry, and handoff rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: fail fast with typed context, quarantine a flaky test, pause producers, shed optional work, reduce concurrency, use a dead-letter or manual review path, roll back a change, or narrow the evidence question This changes how the section resolves when a failed evidence, test, tool, or runtime operation may be retried and what mechanism prevents retries from hiding deterministic defects or amplifying load.

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records sources, proof commands, latency percentiles, errors, timeouts, retries, saturation, rollback triggers, and compact journal evidence, but it does not connect telemetry to Rust callers, typed errors, spawned-task ownership, cancellation, queue capacity, lock contention, features, toolchains, or secret handling
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because observability is useful when an event can be mapped back to a design obligation; raw logs or aggregate timing cannot reveal a detached task, erased error cause, wrong feature set, or hidden caller contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: debug strings become the schema, payloads or secrets are logged, task IDs have no parent, error counts merge causes, percentiles omit workload and sample size, queue saturation lacks capacity, or telemetry exists only on the happy path
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: libraries should not impose service telemetry policy, and this checklist does not replace privacy review, incident response, or production SLO design
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to turn the generic list into an obligation-linked telemetry and journal schema with Rust runtime fields, redaction rules, path coverage, cardinality limits, and response ownership
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that good Rust observability is an executable shadow of ownership and error design: it should make task lifetime, resource pressure, and failure propagation visible without exposing domain data
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record artifact and revision identity, source boundary, requirement and caller, toolchain and target, features, command and fixture, typed error category and source chain, task parentage and shutdown result, queue depth and capacity, lock contention where relevant, latency and allocation only for claimed paths, rollback trigger, owner, and redacted unresolved risk
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because observability is useful when an event can be mapped back to a design obligation; raw logs or aggregate timing cannot reveal a detached task, erased error cause, wrong feature set, or hidden caller contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; debug strings become the schema, payloads or secrets are logged, task IDs have no parent, error counts merge causes, percentiles omit workload and sample size, queue saturation lacks capacity, or telemetry exists only on the happy path
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: libraries should not impose service telemetry policy, and this checklist does not replace privacy review, incident response, or production SLO design
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: turn the generic list into an obligation-linked telemetry and journal schema with Rust runtime fields, redaction rules, path coverage, cardinality limits, and response ownership
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies good Rust observability is an executable shadow of ownership and error design: it should make task lifetime, resource pressure, and failure propagation visible without exposing domain data
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: fields have stable names and units, cardinality is bounded, correlation follows one operation across effects, cancellation and terminal states are distinguishable, sensitive inputs are redacted, and dashboards or journal summaries drive a named action
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because observability is useful when an event can be mapped back to a design obligation; raw logs or aggregate timing cannot reveal a detached task, erased error cause, wrong feature set, or hidden caller contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where debug strings become the schema, payloads or secrets are logged, task IDs have no parent, error counts merge causes, percentiles omit workload and sample size, queue saturation lacks capacity, or telemetry exists only on the happy path
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by libraries should not impose service telemetry policy, and this checklist does not replace privacy review, incident response, or production SLO design
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in fields have stable names and units, cardinality is bounded, correlation follows one operation across effects, cancellation and terminal states are distinguishable, sensitive inputs are redacted, and dashboards or journal summaries drive a named action
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that good Rust observability is an executable shadow of ownership and error design: it should make task lifetime, resource pressure, and failure propagation visible without exposing domain data
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: debug strings become the schema, payloads or secrets are logged, task IDs have no parent, error counts merge causes, percentiles omit workload and sample size, queue saturation lacks capacity, or telemetry exists only on the happy path
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are Display versus Debug leaking data, span guards crossing await unexpectedly, sampling away rare terminal failures, panic paths bypassing normal events, metrics labels built from user input, feature-gated instrumentation, and clock distortion in short benchmarks
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where fields have stable names and units, cardinality is bounded, correlation follows one operation across effects, cancellation and terminal states are distinguishable, sensitive inputs are redacted, and dashboards or journal summaries drive a named action

- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: use test assertions and structured command summaries for libraries, tracing spans for services, bounded event samples for high-volume paths, or a temporary diagnostic build with an expiry and removal gate
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the corpus does not select a tracing implementation, metric backend, sampling rate, retention policy, privacy classification, or service alert threshold
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: use test assertions and structured command summaries for libraries, tracing spans for services, bounded event samples for high-volume paths, or a temporary diagnostic build with an expiry and removal gate

### Question 07: What do good, bad, and borderline examples look like?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the operational comparison is Good: a worker span records parent task, bounded queue occupancy, typed terminal result, cancellation reason, toolchain, and feature set without payload contents. Bad: log every request body and report average latency. Borderline: a library emits no runtime telemetry but supplies executable examples, typed errors, and caller-visible diagnostics
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the good case is credible because fields have stable names and units, cardinality is bounded, correlation follows one operation across effects, cancellation and terminal states are distinguishable, sensitive inputs are redacted, and dashboards or journal summaries drive a named action

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 08 on verification method: verification should also test the consequence that good Rust observability is an executable shadow of ownership and error design: it should make task lifetime, resource pressure, and failure propagation visible without exposing domain data
### Question 09: What is known confidently, and what remains judgment or uncertainty?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the confident evidence is the local checklist explicitly recommends structured tracing at key boundaries and forbids secrets, while the seed supplies source, command, latency, error, timeout, retry, saturation, rollback, and compact-audit signals

### Question 10: What deeper deductions, second-order consequences, or additional insights follow, and how should they change the guidance?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that good Rust observability is an executable shadow of ownership and error design: it should make task lifetime, resource pressure, and failure propagation visible without exposing domain data
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from observability is useful when an event can be mapped back to a design obligation; raw logs or aggregate timing cannot reveal a detached task, erased error cause, wrong feature set, or hidden caller contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where debug strings become the schema, payloads or secrets are logged, task IDs have no parent, error counts merge causes, percentiles omit workload and sample size, queue saturation lacks capacity, or telemetry exists only on the happy path
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within libraries should not impose service telemetry policy, and this checklist does not replace privacy review, incident response, or production SLO design
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: turn the generic list into an obligation-linked telemetry and journal schema with Rust runtime fields, redaction rules, path coverage, cardinality limits, and response ownership
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: use test assertions and structured command summaries for libraries, tracing spans for services, bounded event samples for high-volume paths, or a temporary diagnostic build with an expiry and removal gate This changes how the section resolves which review and runtime observations are needed to confirm that the chosen Rust idioms preserve the documented API, failure, ownership, and lifecycle model.

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed properly requests memory, panic, concurrency, workload, tool-call, latency, and reviewer-decision evidence, but its universal local p95 below 10 ms is unsupported and mixes runtime performance with documentation workflow efficiency
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Rust optimizations change ownership and abstraction costs, while compiler settings, allocator, CPU scheduling, runtime flavor, feature resolution, and input shape can dominate measurements
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a debug build supports a production claim, averages hide tails, one run supplies precision, dead-code elimination removes work, fixtures exclude errors or contention, allocations are inferred from clones, or faster code weakens cancellation and readability without requirement value
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: microbenchmarks support only the measured operation and environment; production capacity, distributed latency, cost, and service objectives need system-level evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to remove the universal 10 ms gate, separate code-runtime and review-workflow metrics, and add a reproducible claim-to-benchmark protocol with correctness, variance, alternative, and rollback checks
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that performance evidence is strongest when it can reject an optimization as unnecessary or contract-damaging, not only when it can celebrate a faster number
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to start from a named requirement and representative operation, define workload and data distribution, baseline and comparison, toolchain and target, build profile and features, runtime topology, warmup and repetitions, latency or throughput statistic, allocation or memory metric when relevant, correctness guard, variance, regression threshold, and reproducible command

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a debug build supports a production claim, averages hide tails, one run supplies precision, dead-code elimination removes work, fixtures exclude errors or contention, allocations are inferred from clones, or faster code weakens cancellation and readability without requirement value
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: microbenchmarks support only the measured operation and environment; production capacity, distributed latency, cost, and service objectives need system-level evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: remove the universal 10 ms gate, separate code-runtime and review-workflow metrics, and add a reproducible claim-to-benchmark protocol with correctness, variance, alternative, and rollback checks

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed correctly stops at multiple systems, unbounded discovery, production traffic without an SLO, distributed file ownership, context drift, and an unnarrowed large codebase, but saying more than one ownership boundary is automatically out of scope would exclude ordinary useful Rust reviews
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because scale becomes unsafe when evidence and rollback no longer fit one coherent obligation set, not merely when code contains several borrows, tasks, modules, or ownership transfers
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a monolithic packet hides independent failure domains, parallel owners edit the same artifact, a split severs caller-to-callee evidence, production advice proceeds without traffic objectives, or decomposition is triggered solely by line count
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this checklist may remain one input after routing, but it must not claim ownership of deployment choreography, distributed consistency, threat modeling, or organization-wide compatibility
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the one-ownership-boundary cutoff with evidence-closure criteria, enumerate escalation triggers and decomposition axes, and add integration ownership plus re-entry checks
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the governing scale metric is evidence closure: a change is too large for this reference when no reviewer can connect every recommendation to its affected contract, failure path, and recovery unit
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to continue while one owner can enumerate affected contracts and verify their callers, errors, task lifecycles, dependencies, features, and rollback; split or route when independent services or runtimes, unsafe or FFI boundaries, public ecosystem compatibility, cross-team migrations, unbounded source graphs, production SLOs, security threats, or irreducible feature matrices prevent that closure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because scale becomes unsafe when evidence and rollback no longer fit one coherent obligation set, not merely when code contains several borrows, tasks, modules, or ownership transfers

- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace the one-ownership-boundary cutoff with evidence-closure criteria, enumerate escalation triggers and decomposition axes, and add integration ownership plus re-entry checks

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local-corpus, external-research, and combined-inference labels but gives no claim-level locator, provenance status, conflict rule, confidence update, freshness rule, or treatment for identical archived copies and unverified public links
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because source labels alone do not prevent a paraphrase from becoming broader than its source or an archived duplicate from being mistaken for independent corroboration
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: two byte-identical copies are counted as two authorities, a retained URL is described as current without opening it, an inference inherits the certainty of a source fact, a generic best practice receives local status, or a benchmark threshold appears without data
